<div id="review_610040882" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610040882" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4731410-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387526203p2/4731410.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/610040882?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/4731410-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780979074974" href="/book/show/7698251-grave-peril">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=magic-and-witchcraft">magic-and-witchcraft</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer610040882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11297687700844526676"><b>Grave Peril</b><br/>3 Stars<br/><br/>Many have stated that <b>Grave Peril</b> is the turning point in the series for the better. After considering the plot and the characters, I must confess that I found <b>Fool Moon</b> to be far more entertaining. <br/><br/>Don't get me wrong. Harry and his quirks are very endearing but a number of issues irritated me in this installment. First, Murphy barely makes an appearance and the absence of a strong willed, take no prisoners, female character detracts from the overall effect of the story. <br/><br/>Second</span>
  <span id="freeText11297687700844526676" style="display:none"><b>Grave Peril</b><br />3 Stars<br /><br />Many have stated that <b>Grave Peril</b> is the turning point in the series for the better. After considering the plot and the characters, I must confess that I found <b>Fool Moon</b> to be far more entertaining. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong. Harry and his quirks are very endearing but a number of issues irritated me in this installment. First, Murphy barely makes an appearance and the absence of a strong willed, take no prisoners, female character detracts from the overall effect of the story. <br /><br />Second, the criticism surrounding Harry's chauvinism finally makes sense. In the first two books, his attitude toward women comes across as gallant and even chivalrous, but the chauvinism is front and center in this one as Harry fixates on the breasts and luscious curves of virtually every female character - is this really necessary? <br /><br />Third, while the basic plot is compelling and the action scenes exciting, the execution is repetitive. How many times must Harry battle the Nightmare before he defeats it? How many times must he get round the machinations of his fairy Godmother? How many times must he be exposed to the lustful effects of vampire venom? How many times must his powers fail him precisely when he needs them the most? Come on already, get some new material. <br /><br />Finally, Harry constantly blames himself for the choices others make that get them into trouble. While this overdeveloped sense of guilt may have its place in the portrayal of Harry's internal struggle with his own conscience, it starts to grate on the nerves after a while. <br /><br />On a more positive note, the secondary characters both old and new are very engaging. Michael, a Knight of the Cross, constitutes an intriguing counterpoint to Harry's irreligious personality, and the manner in which Butcher depicts the power of Christian artifacts adds another layer of complexity to the world building. That said, Michael is a little too self-righteous and condescending for my tastes. <br /><br />There are also some poignant moments between Harry and his reporter girlfriend, Susan Rodriguez, although her misguided Lois Lane routine is getting old and she has never really appealed to me as Harry's love interest.<br /><br />The most interesting characters, however, are Lea, Harry's rather scary fairy Godmother, who serves as a cautionary tale about what happens when one makes ill advised bargains with the fae, and Thomas, the morally ambiguous vampire who plays a pivotal role in Harry's conflict with the various villains in the story. <br /><br />All in all, the world building is strong, the story has potential and the unanswered questions are interesting enough to keep on with the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11297687700844526676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jody " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41767362-jody"><img alt="Jody " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558120407p2/41767362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1640585575?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody " href="/user/show/41767362-jody">Jody </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/13511897-grave-peril">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=top-priority">top-priority</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1640585575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17142745670742127096"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Some words have a power that has nothing to do with supernatural forces. They resound in the heart and mind, they live long after the sounds of them have died away, they echo in the heart and the soul. They have power, and that power is very real.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I will make this review short and sweet. <i>Grave Peril</i> was the best book in <i>The Dresden Files</i> series so far. I know I am only 3 books in, but each one seems to up the stakes and be more exciting than the last. The first two books were light h</span>
  <span id="freeText17142745670742127096" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Some words have a power that has nothing to do with supernatural forces. They resound in the heart and mind, they live long after the sounds of them have died away, they echo in the heart and the soul. They have power, and that power is very real.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I will make this review short and sweet. <i>Grave Peril</i> was the best book in <i>The Dresden Files</i> series so far. I know I am only 3 books in, but each one seems to up the stakes and be more exciting than the last. The first two books were light hearted and fun. But this one took on a little more serious tone toward the middle and end. Not that there weren't any light hearted and fun parts, because it just wouldn't be Harry Dresden without them. I guess the best way to describe it is this. It felt like the real story within the story is beginning to take shape in this installment. <br /><br />The side characters are always enjoyable in these books, and I like how Butcher adds new ones every volume. They are all vastly different and have their own affect on Harry and the plot. It helps to keep things fresh. The reader doesn't have to worry about seeing too much of a character they don't enjoy. Because the odds are, they probably won't be in the next book anyway. Or at least not in as big a role. I haven't had that problem so far, but who knows in future books. <br /><br />I won't say anything about the plot in this book. Just know there are plenty of ghosts and creatures that kick the shit out of Harry. He gets pissed off and starts kicking them back. That is probably the best review of a Harry Dresden plot ever BTW. I seriously can't get enough of these books at the moment. Next up...<i>Summer Knight</i>.<br /><br /><b>Actual Rating: 4.5 stars ****</b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17142745670742127096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10604330816074529066">There seems to be a common idea amongst fans and new arrivals alike to this series, that this, the third book in the series, is where it starts to get good. I’ve read the series and started again while I’m waiting for the next volume- I think the first two are great too. This one just ramps up the action and its consequences. And this might be the one where Harry Dresden starts to slip-by his own standards- taking actions and committing deeds that in an ideal world he would not have chosen to do</span>
  <span id="freeText10604330816074529066" style="display:none">There seems to be a common idea amongst fans and new arrivals alike to this series, that this, the third book in the series, is where it starts to get good. I’ve read the series and started again while I’m waiting for the next volume- I think the first two are great too. This one just ramps up the action and its consequences. And this might be the one where Harry Dresden starts to slip-by his own standards- taking actions and committing deeds that in an ideal world he would not have chosen to do. Harry is the ultimate underdog in a way. He’s always up against impossible odds, often achieving impossible feats with very little in the way of resources. This book is a game changer in terms of the overall story arc and in terms of characters new to the scene as well as character development of established players. Another great read.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12652938413250465242"><b>Author Imbroglio! Plus Five Ring of Imagination used to Write Novel! "(Shakes head) What are the rest of us authors to do?"</b><br/><br/>I assume that Jim Butcher is in possession of a magical ring of imagination +5. He probably wears a cloak of protection vs plot holes and has boots of leaping narrative chasms.<br/><br/>In all honesty, I'm impressed with his writing, however I'm going to ping this book a star for losing my engagement. It lacked the power to fully immerse me in the otherwise dazzling magical world of C</span>
  <span id="freeText12652938413250465242" style="display:none"><b>Author Imbroglio! Plus Five Ring of Imagination used to Write Novel! "(Shakes head) What are the rest of us authors to do?"</b><br /><br />I assume that Jim Butcher is in possession of a magical ring of imagination +5. He probably wears a cloak of protection vs plot holes and has boots of leaping narrative chasms.<br /><br />In all honesty, I'm impressed with his writing, however I'm going to ping this book a star for losing my engagement. It lacked the power to fully immerse me in the otherwise dazzling magical world of Chicago that Harry inhabits.<br /><br />I think I know what the problem is - it's the villains. From the ghosts to the vampires, they have no depth...<br /><br />Even Harry's faerie godmother is predictable because she's two dimensional.<br /><br />It's a sorry state of affairs when the villains lack charisma.<br /><br /><b> Recommended with a caveat: '4 Two-Dimensional Villains at Six O'clock,' stars. </b></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2240603171" />
    <a title="JHollywood " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12467413-jhollywood"><img alt="JHollywood " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517107366p2/12467413.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2240603171?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JHollywood " class="user" itemprop="url" name="JHollywood " href="/user/show/12467413-jhollywood">JHollywood </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2240603171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18195774168883574891">Honestly, i feel like these books keep on getting better and better. It was a fast easy read, that was engaging, funny, and typical Harry Dresden. I really like the direction the series is going. I feel like with every new installment, his writing its becoming more mature and prolific. For me everything is starting to feel a bit more complete and i'm finding it easier to start relating to Harry and the world all around him. I was happy to finally have more contact with the nevernever and more of</span>
  <span id="freeText18195774168883574891" style="display:none">Honestly, i feel like these books keep on getting better and better. It was a fast easy read, that was engaging, funny, and typical Harry Dresden. I really like the direction the series is going. I feel like with every new installment, his writing its becoming more mature and prolific. For me everything is starting to feel a bit more complete and i'm finding it easier to start relating to Harry and the world all around him. I was happy to finally have more contact with the nevernever and more of a multiple narrative that was different from the typical linear style from the previous novels. All in all, it was a fun and fast novel filled with action, hilarity, demons, ghosts, vampires, dragons, Knights, faeries..... what more could you ask for???</span>

<div id="review_1567589035" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567589035" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1567589035?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1567589035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3627295949663615148">I rarely feel the urge to read books in the “urban fantasy” subgenre. An awful lot of them seem to be “paranormal romances” which are anathema to me. I think I have only read a few urban fantasies, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_' title='American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman' rel='nofollow noopener'> American Gods</a>, China Miéville’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6931246.Kraken' title='Kraken by China Miéville' rel='nofollow noopener'> Kraken</a>, and Clive Barker’s classic <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52640.Weaveworld' title='Weaveworld by Clive Barker' rel='nofollow noopener'> Weaveworld</a> spring to mind. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/40346-the-dresden-files' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dresden Files</a> series has quite a reputation though, it has a rabid fan base and it is often recommended in SF/F online forums. However, even fans of the series tend to agree that the first couple of bo</span>
  <span id="freeText3627295949663615148" style="display:none">I rarely feel the urge to read books in the “urban fantasy” subgenre. An awful lot of them seem to be “paranormal romances” which are anathema to me. I think I have only read a few urban fantasies, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_" title="American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener"> American Gods</a>, China Miéville’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6931246.Kraken" title="Kraken by China Miéville" rel="nofollow noopener"> Kraken</a>, and Clive Barker’s classic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52640.Weaveworld" title="Weaveworld by Clive Barker" rel="nofollow noopener"> Weaveworld</a> spring to mind. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40346-the-dresden-files" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dresden Files</a> series has quite a reputation though, it has a rabid fan base and it is often recommended in SF/F online forums. However, even fans of the series tend to agree that the first couple of books in the series are not so great, and the series really pick up in hook #3, <i>Grave Peril</i>. I can’t speak for book #2, but I did read the first book of the series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47212.Storm_Front__The_Dresden_Files___1_" title="Storm Front (The Dresden Files, #1) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener"> Storm Front</a>, and I was not impressed. Still, if a series is enormously popular and it deserves a second chance, though probably not a third one, so I skipped book #2, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/91477.Fool_Moon__The_Dresden_Files___2_" title="Fool Moon (The Dresden Files, #2) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener"> Fool Moon</a>.<br /><br />A brief synopsis: Someone is causing an imbalance between our world and the spirit world causing a huge increase in paranormal activities. As a result, one of Harry Dresden’s friends has been driven mad, and another one in a coma. In order to save his friends Harry and a few friends have to battle ghosts, demons, <i>ghosts of demons</i>, and more vampires than you can shake a garlic bread at.<br /> <br />Another reason I seldom read urban fantasy is that—for me—it requires even more suspension of disbelieve than the standard “sword &amp; sorcery” fantasy. The setting is “our world” but with a magical component welded on, so the wizardry and monstrosities goings-on seem just a little ridiculous. I think this is the advantage of sci-fi, we live in a scientific world so even when the science is made-up (or just plain wrong) the fiction often has a ring of plausibility.<br /><br />Having said that, I have to admit I was pretty much sold on <i>Grave Peril</i> from the battle with a ghost a few pages in. It starts with a wonderfully creepy atmosphere and sudden escalation into a magical battle that is so kinetic and intense I forgot how ludicrous the whole premise is. In order to get the most out of the book, I decided to commit to the nonsense and just go along on Jim Butcher’s wild ride. It does help that Butcher is very good at his chosen field, the internal logic or “magic system” that he employs is consistent and believable within the setting he creates. Also, the pacing of the book is so fast that my habitual disbelief has no time to surface. <br /><br />Then there is the characterization.<br /><i>“But I’m a sucker for a lady in distress. I always have been. It’s a weak point in my character, a streak of chivalry a mile wide and twice as deep.”</i><br />I have had enough of anti-heroes, but a flawed hero with his heart in the right place is someone I can get behind. His sidekick Michael Carpenter, a “Knight of the Cross”, is also very interesting. If he was the protagonist of the series, it would probably have fallen under the “Christian fiction” label.<br /><i>“He’s a righteous man.” <br />“He seemed nice enough to me.” <br />“No, not self-righteous. Righteous. The real deal. He’s honest, loyal, faithful. He lives his ideals. It gives him power.””</i><br /><br />The pacing of the book is quite relentless and it almost never slows down to take a breather. Harry faces one crisis after another and <i>almost</i> dies every time, and more often than not he survives by coming up with outlandish solutions that sometimes feel like deus ex machina. The continuous battling does become a little repetitious by the end of the book but never actually boring, thanks to Jim Butcher’s narrative skills. If I say “turn your brain off and enjoy this book” it would sound like a backhanded compliment that implies the book is stupid. It maybe silly, but it is certainly not stupid. Jim Butcher put a lot of thoughts into his world building, characterization and plotting, but it seems like he has done all the heavy lifting and the reader does not need to make any real effort to follow the story. <br /><br />By the end of the book, I felt quite satisfied and look forward to reading many more of Harry Dresden's ridiculous adventures.<br />___________________<br /><br /><b>Worldbuilding Quotes: </b><br />These are examples of Jim Butcher's elaborate world building rather than passages of literary beauty (of which there is none, it's not that kind of book).<br /><br /><i>“Not a house,”I said. “A home. There’s a difference.”“So what about Victor Sells’s place? I hear you took him on, right?”I shook my head. “He’d screwed up his threshold. He was running his business out of it, using the place for dark ceremonies. It wasn’t a home anymore.”<br /><br />In the circles of the supernatural community, an Old World code of conduct still ruled. When you have a problem, you settle it face to face, within the circle.<br /><br />Working magic directly on a human body is difficult. It’s very difficult. Conjuring up forces, like my shield, or elemental manifestations like the fire or wind is a snap compared to the complexity and power required to change someone’s hair a different color—or to cause the cells on either side of an injury to fuse back together, closing it.”</i><br />___________________<br /><b>Funny Quotes:</b><br /><i>“Dead before the sun rises,” I said. “Stars, Bob, why don’t you just go all the way over the melodramatic edge and tell me that I’m going to be sleeping with the fishes?” “I’m not sure that much of you would be left,” Bob said,<br /><br />“Well,” Thomas said. “I’d like to see this. I’ve never seen an external transformation before. Do proceed, madame.” He waved his hand impatiently. “Dog him, already!”</i><br /><br />(There are many more of course).</span>
  <a data-text-id="3627295949663615148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6708475465999243501">WOW, what a great book !!!<br/>Fool Moon was much better than Storm Front, and Grave Peril is even better than Fool Moon.The series is definitely getting better and evolves to something bigger and very engaging,no doubt that Jim Butcher is a great author. That's an action packed book with lots of humor,magic and great characters. I really liked Harry's Godmother and Michael as a new characters, Harry and Bob are great (as usual).<br/><br/>Highly recommended !!!<br/></span>

<div id="review_1864460130" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1864460130" />
    <a title="Lena K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46184829-lena-k"><img alt="Lena K." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559055379p2/46184829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1864460130?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lena K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lena K." href="/user/show/46184829-lena-k">Lena K.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/7021986-grave-peril">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46184829-lena-k?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1864460130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15916770567930819622"><b>
  <i>“Holy shit”, I breathed. “Hellhounds.”<br/>“Harry”, Michael said sternly. “You know I hate it when you swear.”<br/>“You're right. Sorry. Holy shit”, I breathed, “heckhounds.”</i>
</b><br/> <br/>I actually really liked this one! Harry is still sexist and chauvinist, and still describes women by the shape of their boobs (COME ON ALREADY, it’s getting old...) but holly heck! We have an evil fairy godmother with hell hounds, an egotistic dragon, evil vampire brothers, a girl with prophetic dreams that no one believes to, cr</span>
  <span id="freeText15916770567930819622" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Holy shit”, I breathed. “Hellhounds.”<br />“Harry”, Michael said sternly. “You know I hate it when you swear.”<br />“You're right. Sorry. Holy shit”, I breathed, “heckhounds.”</i>
</b><br /> <br />I actually really liked this one! Harry is still sexist and chauvinist, and still describes women by the shape of their boobs (COME ON ALREADY, it’s getting old...) but holly heck! We have an evil fairy godmother with hell hounds, an egotistic dragon, evil vampire brothers, a girl with prophetic dreams that no one believes to, crazy ghosts, faith magic and cool swords! YAS. Did I mention court intrigue? YES please.<br /><br />I like Harry because he’s very human, with human flaws that get him in trouble. He’s not always the sharpest or smartest, he does stupid things and makes bad decisions. But his heart is in the right place. <br /><br />What I don’t like is that he always, ALWAYS ends up unconscious or hurt beyond repair, his vision always swims, his stomach always churns, he always wants to (or does) throw up, ENOUGH with that, it’s annoying and not very believable that he’s always on the brink of death, but never actually dies, *sigh*.<br /><br />The plot and mystery were actually very captivating and the humor good as always.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“I still can't believe”, Michael said, “that you came to the Vampires' Masquerade Ball dressed as a vampire.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I’m looking forward reading the next one.</span>

<div id="review_1307516315" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1307516315" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1307516315?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/7021986-grave-peril">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1307516315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17425922453778894399">Grave Peril was such a mixed bag that I actually felt disoriented when I finished it. <br/><br/>The plot started out strong and I was completely engrossed during the first half of the book. However, in the end, I found the plot to be overly strung out and convoluted to be convincing. Everything that which culminated into the climax just seemed too elaborate a set-up and Harry's resolutions to the endless stream of dire situations he got himself into begun to appear far-fetched, and even convenient at time</span>
  <span id="freeText17425922453778894399" style="display:none">Grave Peril was such a mixed bag that I actually felt disoriented when I finished it. <br /><br />The plot started out strong and I was completely engrossed during the first half of the book. However, in the end, I found the plot to be overly strung out and convoluted to be convincing. Everything that which culminated into the climax just seemed too elaborate a set-up and Harry's resolutions to the endless stream of dire situations he got himself into begun to appear far-fetched, and even convenient at times. <br /><br />While I had issues with the plot, the expansionary paranormal worldbuilding and development of Harry's character continued to be the highlight of the series. The spooky ghosts, the mysterious Fae, and the intriguing vampire court were all completely riveting, as was the unexpected knowledge of the identity of Harry's godmother. This revelation really opened up a whole new dimension to Harry's back story which begs to be explored further. <br /><br />Character development kicked up a notch in this instalment. While Murphy didn't feature much in this instalment, there was a compelling and touching moment when Harry's wizard Sight revealed her in a spectacular manner. Harry’s relationship with Susan also finally took a romantic turn, hitting both a high- and low-point, in the span of just this single volume. <br /><br />Harry gained a sidekick, so to speak, from a new character, Michael Carpenter - a Knight of the Cross who wields Amoracchius, an incredibly powerful object of faith in the form of a sword. Michael seemed a bit too righteous for my liking despite understanding that the strength of his unwavering faith made him into what he is and enables him to utilise the sword effectively. <br /><br />The pacing of the story ensured a strong momentum to keep the reader engaged so even though I had issued with the plot, I can't say that I was ever bored. There will be some serious consequences to our Wizard P.I. post the climactic events at the end of this instalment so while I both enjoyed and felt frustrated with this read, my curiosity and love for the supernatural should keep me powering through this series for the moment. <br /><br /><i>This review can also be found at <a href="http://booknest.eu/review/ts-reviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Booknest</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17425922453778894399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_113713213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113713213" />
    <a title="Jordan Price" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2709426-jordan-price"><img alt="Jordan Price" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442462666p2/2709426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113713213?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jordan Price" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jordan Price" href="/user/show/2709426-jordan-price">Jordan Price</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113713213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10932814760447379859">I loved aspects of this story and hated others. I adored the magic, the description of how power worked, how Harry created his spells. I also loved how he got put through the wringer and had to really be willing to sacrifice himself for the survival of the people he loved.<br/><br/>I hated the female characters. I hated that their breasts were described at every available opportunity, particularly the villains. During a climactic fight scene, a female villain was "distracted" by a vampire sliding his hand</span>
  <span id="freeText10932814760447379859" style="display:none">I loved aspects of this story and hated others. I adored the magic, the description of how power worked, how Harry created his spells. I also loved how he got put through the wringer and had to really be willing to sacrifice himself for the survival of the people he loved.<br /><br />I hated the female characters. I hated that their breasts were described at every available opportunity, particularly the villains. During a climactic fight scene, a female villain was "distracted" by a vampire sliding his hands under her top, and I thought, "Yes, of course the story had to go there." Susan, the girlfriend character, walks into danger and puts everyone else in danger with such willfully ignorant and selfish motives I could scream. (She is supposed to be smart, so why does she do something so moronic?) I feel like the women are all selfish sex objects.<br /><br />The writing technique is mostly clean and conversational with a few dips into purple prose, but I noticed the tendency to hurtle up to a tipping point, end the chapter, and then draw way, way back into a philosophical musing at the beginning of the next chapter rather than continuing with the action. I would have liked that on occasion, but not chapter after chapter.<br /><br />So even though I rated it a three (because of the icky representation of women), I really loved certain elements of the book, and reading the way it was worded and constructed helped me wrap my head around the way I approach writing myself, what works for me and what doesn't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10932814760447379859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26080528" />
    <a title="Doreen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1235896-doreen"><img alt="Doreen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348630486p2/1235896.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26080528?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doreen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doreen" href="/user/show/1235896-doreen">Doreen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/1290386.Grave_Peril">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26080528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17749015806897551426">I will probably have to find a print version, as I kept getting distracted from the story and am fairly certain I missed huge chunks of plot. My boyfriend found this gripping and has taken to listening to it on his own, but I personally found myself irritated by Harry. Honestly, he behaves too much like the stock hero of a romance novel, only with wizardly powers. Speaking of stock, am I the only person unimpressed by the story-line? It's a fairly middling urban fantasy plot: I actually preferre</span>
  <span id="freeText17749015806897551426" style="display:none">I will probably have to find a print version, as I kept getting distracted from the story and am fairly certain I missed huge chunks of plot. My boyfriend found this gripping and has taken to listening to it on his own, but I personally found myself irritated by Harry. Honestly, he behaves too much like the stock hero of a romance novel, only with wizardly powers. Speaking of stock, am I the only person unimpressed by the story-line? It's a fairly middling urban fantasy plot: I actually preferred Fool Moon. The only good thing about the plot, for me, was how much time Murphy spent unconscious. Harry might irritate me, but Murphy makes me glad she's a fictional character, because she is too obnoxious to live.<br /><br />Also, I love James Marsters and could listen to him talk to me for hours, but if he has to say Hell's Bells ONE more time, I may be tempted to punch him. Or Jim Butcher, who deserves it more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17749015806897551426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dNzMfJy+0HAbSy994Wl5Hj6tBOXdLrxkUGquIsdJq7JTRc8pYThzhkeNHkpbapOWeVwNVrUFetHz4DWgngu5ug==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2vsRXBYwmSdL1W81Sakg8RsffbXuZ/b7y0oZhOnxYPb9YhIJ67Y60RcTXgLzqsp5XO50BoZMME5owIIGsLNy/g==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer7778677067026222211">Jim Butcher is the author of the Dresden Files, the Codex Alera, and a new steampunk series, the Cinder Spires. His resume includes a laundry list of skills which were useful a couple of centuries ago, and he plays guitar quite badly.   <span id="freeText7778677067026222211" style="display:none">Jim Butcher is the author of the Dresden Files, the Codex Alera, and a new steampunk series, the Cinder Spires. His resume includes a laundry list of skills which were useful a couple of centuries ago, and he plays guitar quite badly. An avid gamer, he plays tabletop games in varying systems, a variety of video games on PC and console, and LARPs whenever he can make time for it. Jim currently resides mostly inside his own head, but his head can generally be found in his home town of Independence, Missouri.<br /><br />Jim goes by the moniker Longshot in a number of online locales. He came by this name in the early 1990′s when he decided he would become a published author. Usually only 3 in 1000 who make such an attempt actually manage to become published; of those, only 1 in 10 make enough money to call it a living. The sale of a second series was the breakthrough that let him beat the long odds against attaining a career as a novelist.<br /><br />All the same, he refuses to change his nickname.<br /></span>
